  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_af66e55b-5073-4321-a33d-968a2fe185b8'

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Hi Irene - I think Leon is either black, brown or mixed race. As Aesha said before, that wouldn't stop him from being Irish. In the scene where the pi<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Hi Irene - I think Leon is either black, brown or mixed race. As Aesha said before, that wouldn't stop him from being Irish. In the scene where the pictures of him as a 'model' are published in the Daily Mail, Tiffy mentions that there are racist comments underneath. I was a little confused, because him being described as 'light brown' didn't immediately lead me to think he was a person of colour. (I'm 'brown' myself, being a Brit of Indian origin).<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30036082-warda?shelf=reread-worthy">reread-worthy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30036082-warda?shelf=characters-of-colour">characters-of-colour</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30036082-warda?shelf=library-reads">library-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30036082-warda?shelf=i-fell-in-love">i-fell-in-love</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2740616136" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11173480771430821999">And here you are, book, going on my favourites list. <br/><br/>This was a pleasant surprise in the best way possible. I knew that I would enjoy it, but I fell in love instead. <br/><br/>It’s a quiet, heartwarming story that follows Tiffy and Leon. Both have agreed on an unusual arrangement between themselves and are sharing not only a flat, but a bed together. But they don’t see each other. Tiffy has the apartment to herself in the evenings, and when she’s off to work, that’s when Leon comes home. <br/><br/>During this arran</span>
  <span id="freeText11173480771430821999" style="display:none">And here you are, book, going on my favourites list. <br /><br />This was a pleasant surprise in the best way possible. I knew that I would enjoy it, but I fell in love instead. <br /><br />It’s a quiet, heartwarming story that follows Tiffy and Leon. Both have agreed on an unusual arrangement between themselves and are sharing not only a flat, but a bed together. But they don’t see each other. Tiffy has the apartment to herself in the evenings, and when she’s off to work, that’s when Leon comes home. <br /><br />During this arrangement, they exchange very simple, ordinary notes that are left around the apartment and slowly their lives starts to intertwine without them meaning to. <br /><br />I was expecting something fluffy and cute and whilst those elements were there, the underlying tone of the story was a lot more serious. They’re dealing with their own demons and struggles and are on survival mode, till that fails them. <br />It all felt very realistic, and honest and true to real life. <br /><br />I just loved everything about this story, the format it was told in, the alternate POVs, how well we got to know the characters and how much it meant to me to see them succeed. It was quirky, clever and Tiffy and Leon’s personalities shined through the writing. I was in their world whilst reading and wanted to be a part of their world. <br /> <br />I’m already missing these characters. I know I won’t forget them anytime soon. <br /><br />It’s amazing that this is a debut novel. I need more of Beth O’Leary’s stories in my life. <br /><br />———————————<br /><br />I’ve got 3 days to read this before I have to return it to the library. <br /><br />(self-made) Challenge accepted.</span>

          </span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2741042842?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nilufer Ozmekik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nilufer Ozmekik" href="/user/show/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik">Nilufer Ozmekik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/41150287-the-flatshare">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/53701594-nilufer-ozmekik?shelf=boring">boring</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2741042842" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14751986464154605802">Three dull, unsatisfied stars gave my shiny place in the minority among the readers who gave so much stars to this one⭐️⭐️⭐️<br/>I mostly like chic-lit books especially written by Irish and British writers. I like Marian Keyes’ books which shouldn’t be defined as soft chic lit ones because of the characters’ heavy baggages and emotional problems ( alcoholism, denial the dead of loved ones, abuse victims)<br/>On this book our heroine Tiffi suffers from emotional abuse and with flashbacks of her relationshi</span>
  <span id="freeText14751986464154605802" style="display:none">Three dull, unsatisfied stars gave my shiny place in the minority among the readers who gave so much stars to this one⭐️⭐️⭐️<br />I mostly like chic-lit books especially written by Irish and British writers. I like Marian Keyes’ books which shouldn’t be defined as soft chic lit ones because of the characters’ heavy baggages and emotional problems ( alcoholism, denial the dead of loved ones, abuse victims)<br />On this book our heroine Tiffi suffers from emotional abuse and with flashbacks of her relationship she starts to realize she was gaslighted by her ex’s manipulative lies. But the way of storytelling about the heroine’s trauma wasn’t strong enough, it didn’t make me feel sorry for her. I found her emotional turmoil a little superficial and unreliable.<br /><br />And of course I didn’t like our hero so much. I found him a little indecisive, passive, boring. At the end as soon as he thought he was rejected by heroine, he just gave up and he never showed how he felt about her. He never wanted to meet her at first because he had issues about changing things in his life( which is ridiculous excuse) then as soon as he discovered she had a great body, he asked for a date !!!<br /><br />The things I liked most are: hero and heroine’s communication way with post its.<br />And supporting characters Richie and Rachel( they deserve their own book)<br /><br />Maybe I read too many angsty books lately so I increased my pain level and this book was too soft, painless and a little boring for me.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2868810476" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2868810476" />
    <a title="jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica"><img alt="jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1509983330p2/10171516.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2868810476?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="jessica" href="/user/show/10171516-jessica">jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/51558034-the-flatshare">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2868810476" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11648461830410928167">this story really grew on me, in the best way possible. i guess its true what they say, that opposites attract, because a couple of things that would normally be off-putting to me as a reader (tiffy being stereotypically ‘quirky’ and the odd writing/formatting of leons chapters) turned out to be very endearing and made me enjoy the story that much more. <br/><br/>i love how this radiated british humour. its so understated, undervalued even, and i thought leon was hilarious. both characters are charming an</span>
  <span id="freeText11648461830410928167" style="display:none">this story really grew on me, in the best way possible. i guess its true what they say, that opposites attract, because a couple of things that would normally be off-putting to me as a reader (tiffy being stereotypically ‘quirky’ and the odd writing/formatting of leons chapters) turned out to be very endearing and made me enjoy the story that much more. <br /><br />i love how this radiated british humour. its so understated, undervalued even, and i thought leon was hilarious. both characters are charming and i thought tiffy went through an amazing character development. for being a light and fluffy book, there are some quite serious topics discussed in this, mainly emotional abuse and manipulation; but i thought it was handled really well, in a way that was loyal and realistic to the characters and story. <br /><br />overall, im very much impressed with this debut novel and i think its safe to say beth o’leary is an author to keep an eye on!<br /><br /><b>↠ <i>3.5 stars</i></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="11648461830410928167" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2744222921" />
    <a title="✨ A ✨ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/65321843-a"><img alt="✨ A ✨ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604503440p2/65321843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2744222921?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/43315814-the-flatshare">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=faves-adult-romance">faves-adult-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=2019-release">2019-release</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/65321843-a?shelf=all-the-stars-in-the-sky">all-the-stars-in-the-sky</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2744222921" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4593965506259155492"><b>
  <i>It’s weird how easily you can get to know someone from the traces they leave behind.</i>
</b><br/><br/>The best kinds of books are those that surprise you with their perfection. I was expecting this to be a cutesy light hearted read. It was and it wasn't. The characters were more complex than I had anticipated and so was the plot. <br/><br/>Tiffy is desperate for a place to live and Leon is short on cash. They come to an odd arrangement. They will share not only a flat but the same bed. Leon has the flat for the day unt</span>
  <span id="freeText4593965506259155492" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>It’s weird how easily you can get to know someone from the traces they leave behind.</i>
</b><br /><br />The best kinds of books are those that surprise you with their perfection. I was expecting this to be a cutesy light hearted read. It was and it wasn't. The characters were more complex than I had anticipated and so was the plot. <br /><br />Tiffy is desperate for a place to live and Leon is short on cash. They come to an odd arrangement. They will share not only a flat but the same bed. Leon has the flat for the day until he starts his shift at the hospital and Tiffy gets it at night. But the strangest part of the arrangement is that they never meet. What starts as leaving a note to remember to leave the toilet seat down turns into a correspondence between friends. <br /><br />Both have their own life problems to deal with and it was so beautiful to see how they supported and helped one another. <br /><br />A book with a written correspondence between the main characters are one of my favourite kinds. Be it email or letter or text, I just love seeing how two people can form a bond withought having seen each other. <br /><br />Leon's chapters were very different in style. The sentences were shorter and direct and I liked how they conveyed his way of thinking. The two POV's were distinct and I loved how you could clearly tell them apart. While this style of writing probably isn't everyone's cup of tea, I enjoyed the hell out of it. <br /><br />I am so glad I read this. It is being added to my favourites list and I will definitely give it a reread. I can't wait to see what else Beth O'leary has in store for us. <br /><br /><b>TW: EMOTIONAL ABUSE; EMOTIONAL MANIPULATION; STALKING</b><br />_______<br /><br />Pre-weekend buddy read with my gal <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/30036082-warda" rel="nofollow noopener">Warda</a>! 💗</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2668792643" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2668792643" />
    <a title="Emer (A Little Haze)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4629647-emer-a-little-haze"><img alt="Emer (A Little Haze)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589390599p2/4629647.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2668792643?book_show_action=true">Jan 15, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emer (A Little Haze)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emer (A Little Haze)" href="/user/show/4629647-emer-a-little-haze">Emer (A Little Haze)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/43315814-the-flatshare">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=challenge-atoz2019">challenge-atoz2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=4stars">4stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=adult-fiction">adult-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=read2019">read2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=light-fiction">light-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4629647-emer-a-little-haze?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2668792643" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10802031193178911373"><i>now available in both hardback and eBook format in the UK / Ireland</i><br/><br/>Yasssssss!!! Oh I have been waiting for a book like this one to come along FOR YEARS! The Flatshare is exactly what I want from a romantic comedy/dramedy type book... It's got hugely likeable protagonists in the form of Tiffy and Leon, a highly original setup for the meeting of these two characters, a cast of interesting supporting characters and side storylines but most of all... It feels fresh!!! Hallelujah for that. I have fou</span>
  <span id="freeText10802031193178911373" style="display:none"><i>now available in both hardback and eBook format in the UK / Ireland</i><br /><br />Yasssssss!!! Oh I have been waiting for a book like this one to come along FOR YEARS! The Flatshare is exactly what I want from a romantic comedy/dramedy type book... It's got hugely likeable protagonists in the form of Tiffy and Leon, a highly original setup for the meeting of these two characters, a cast of interesting supporting characters and side storylines but most of all... It feels fresh!!! Hallelujah for that. I have found myself getting so jaded when it comes to this genre of book but this one is a veritable diamond in the rough. 'The Flatshare' does not feel like so many of the countless romantic-comedy/dramedy books I've read throughout the years.<br /><br />The setup for this book is a bit bonkers but it really works. Tiffy and Leon are flatmates with a twist. They share a bed! But Leon is in the flat only during the day as he works night shifts. Whereas Tiffy is in the flat at nights and on the weekends. Their lives are so separate that they haven't even met... I mean we know where this is going right? BUT THE JOURNEY IS FABULOUS! Tiffy and Leon start leaving generic post it notes for each other around the flat (regarding things such as bin day, leftover food etc) but these notes gradually evolve into a deeper intimacy and the two find themselves wondering a lot more about the other person and if maybe there is a significant connection. The pacing is perfect btw, I thought the book might have the error of using the notes as the sole point of contact between the two leads for too long, but, the author got it spot on with how she kept building upon their burgeoning relationship. <br /><br />Tiffy is the traditional quirky type of leading lady that we so often get in these books BUT because of the great writing and the fact that she has a fabulous backstory and is a character laden with genuine feelings and emotions, her quirkiness feels authentic to who she is as a person. And who she is is also incredibly relatable. She's got a wonderfully human quality about her and is fabulously dynamic in that at times she's spunky but others is vulnerable and weak. <br /><br />Leon bless him is just lovely. He's so quiet but filled with lots of hidden emotions. The backstory regarding his mum and his brother and how that translates to his chosen career is quite touching to read about. <br /><br />So what I really wasn't expecting is that this story is far more emotional than I ever thought possible from a light read. This is because it deals with some heavy issues regarding destructive and controlling relationships; all of which I thought were handled in quite an appropriate fashion for such an accessible / easy read. <br /><br />And what happily contrasted with that emotional side of the book were a great number of humorous moments. I laughed out loud FREQUENTLY at the fabulous jokes and witty dialogue between the characters. FYI, for those of us who enjoy that sort of thing, there are some fabulous patriarchy bashing jokes in the book that are absolute gems! <br /><br />If you're a fan of romantic comedies and romantic dramadies then this book is definitely one you should pick up when it's published in April 2019. <br /><br /><i><br />*An e-copy of this book was kindly provided to me by the publisher, Quercus, via NetGalley in exchange for an honest review.*</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="10802031193178911373" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2819133563" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2819133563" />
    <a title="Corina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8905971-corina"><img alt="Corina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580618612p2/8905971.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2819133563?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Corina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Corina" href="/user/show/8905971-corina">Corina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8905971-corina?shelf=debut-novel">debut-novel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8905971-corina?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8905971-corina?shelf=british">british</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8905971-corina?shelf=quirky">quirky</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8905971-corina?shelf=rom-com">rom-com</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8905971-corina?shelf=standalone">standalone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8905971-corina?shelf=friends-to-lovers">friends-to-lovers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2819133563" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17432702769415501944">I often lament that romance novels have started to feel the same to me after reading as many as I’ve read over the years. It’s hard for me to distinguish the many novels I read unless they are utterly unique. I’m happy to say, that Beth O’Learly did what I wish many other authors would do, she wrote a debut novel that was quirky, unique and had a most engaging plot.<br/><br/>The Flatshare was a feel-good novel that was hard to forget. Memorable from begging to end, thanks to fabulously vibrant and distinc</span>
  <span id="freeText17432702769415501944" style="display:none">I often lament that romance novels have started to feel the same to me after reading as many as I’ve read over the years. It’s hard for me to distinguish the many novels I read unless they are utterly unique. I’m happy to say, that Beth O’Learly did what I wish many other authors would do, she wrote a debut novel that was quirky, unique and had a most engaging plot.<br><br>The Flatshare was a feel-good novel that was hard to forget. Memorable from begging to end, thanks to fabulously vibrant and distinctive characters and an overall storyline that was heart-touching and beautiful. And this book needs to be read by every romance novel enthusiast out there.<br><br>FACT IS, THAT JUST THE IDEA OF SHARING A FLAT WITH SOMEONE, BUT NEVER CATCHING SIGHT OF THE OTHER PERSON, EVEN THOUGH THEY ARE SHARING A BED WAS ABSOLUTELY INTRIGUING TO ME.<br><br>I think for me the heart and soul of the story was the way Tiffy and Leon communicated with each other. Their post-it notes conversations were heart-warming, funny, touching, and just all around wonderful. A truly refreshing take on a romantic comedy. I actually was looking forward to those notes – maybe even more so than Leon himself.<br><br>Besides their post-it chats, there were three major plots that wove beautifully through the entire story. These plots were connected by a cast of wonderful characters. Every single cast member was distinctively different in personality and voice. And I LOVED them all.<br><br>Both Leon and Tiffy were genuine and nice. Easy to be liked. And a wonderful addition to anyone’s circle of friends. I’m not surprised that they drew me in from almost the very beginning.<br><br>“Almost” because I needed a tiny bit of an adjustment period until I was truly comfortable with the author’s writing style. Not only had the book a distinctive British voice (which I’m a HUGE fan of) but Leon’s POV was quite peculiar. Moreover the author managed to capture the uniqueness of Leon’s personality in an incredibly compelling way.<br><br>HONESTLY, I HAVE ONLY GREAT THINGS TO SAY ABOUT THIS DEBUT NOVEL.<br><br>It might even be one of the most unique novels I read this year. And it definitely goes on my ‘new to me author list of 2019.<br><br>UPDATE: I just recently listened to the audiobook, a year after publication, and I loved the book as much the second time around as I did the first time, in 2019. The audiobook beautifully showcased the Britishness of the novel in the BEST way, and managed to make the narration an entertaining experience.<br>___________________________________<br><br><a href="https://thebrowneyedbookworm.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more reviews and book recommendations on my blog</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebrowneyedbookworm/" rel="nofollow noopener">Follow me on Bookstagram</a><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1587353833i/29323140._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="17432702769415501944" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

In fact I think this is going to go rather badly. <br/><br/>Then I finished it and thought: As I said and as I, a liar, always b</span>
  <span id="freeText6553640616446986684" style="display:none">This book is now a Goodreads Choice Award Nominee for romance, and it's also MY Goodreads Choice for romance, meaning this is very good and I enjoyed reading it and also Goodreads was involved. <br /><br />When I first read the synopsis of this book, I thought: I think I'll like this very much.<br /><br />Then I read a little bit of it and thought: Actually I do not think this is going to go very well. In fact I think this is going to go rather badly. <br /><br />Then I finished it and thought: As I said and as I, a liar, always believed I would, I liked this very much.<br /><br />When I saw this book about two people who don't know each other who share a flat (one has it in the day and one at night), and that they communicate via Post-It notes until they inevitably fall in love (I believe it is impossible to conduct epistolary interactions with someone over a long period of time and not fall in love with them), I believed this would be light and fluffy and adorable and just what I needed.<br /><br />This was not very light. Nor was it very fluffy. Actually it was very stressful and angsty and emotional. But it was what I needed???<br /><br />This is a very heartfelt and well-done story about supportive love and people healing from abuse and trauma and just all around character development joy. But a lot of suffering before we get to the joy part.<br /><br />It is just so very good. SO much better than I expected.<br /><br />Bottom line: LIKE I SAID. MY GOODREADS CHOICE. <br /><br />--------<br /><i>pre-review</i><br /><br />all right, i admit it! i'm swooning!!<br /><br />review to come / 4 stars<br /><br />--------<br /><br />i'm a simple girl. i read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2837251775?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">a scary book</a>, then i immediately read a rom-com to soothe my cowardly soul</span>

<div id="review_2789304155" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2789304155" />
    <a title="Paromjit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38610813-paromjit"><img alt="Paromjit" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2789304155?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paromjit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paromjit" href="/user/show/38610813-paromjit">Paromjit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=humour-comic-fiction">humour-comic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38610813-paromjit?shelf=women-s-fiction">women-s-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2789304155" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14416026680012505172">This is a charming and lovely piece of contemporary fiction from Beth O'Leary that takes an interesting premise of a one bedroom flat in London being shared by two occupants who never meet, each in residence, sleeping in the same bed, when the other is out or working. A more exploitative version of this is the overcrowded sharing of accommodation in the desperate working conditions experienced by trafficked, illegal and migrant workers. This is a more benign and comic take focusing on the dire f</span>
  <span id="freeText14416026680012505172" style="display:none">This is a charming and lovely piece of contemporary fiction from Beth O'Leary that takes an interesting premise of a one bedroom flat in London being shared by two occupants who never meet, each in residence, sleeping in the same bed, when the other is out or working. A more exploitative version of this is the overcrowded sharing of accommodation in the desperate working conditions experienced by trafficked, illegal and migrant workers. This is a more benign and comic take focusing on the dire financial straits many workers face in a city with sky high rents. Compassionate palliative care nurse, Leon Twomey, a man of few words has a girlfriend, Kay, and a younger brother, Richie, in prison after being framed for armed robbery. Leon needs money to pay Richie's lawyer to secure an appeal hearing, so Tiffany 'Tiffy' Moore moves in, and for months they never meet, their paths never cross, but a quirky and offbeat relationship develops between the pair of them through the form of post-it notes.<br /><br />Tiffy is still hankering after her ex-boyfriend, the wealthy and manipulative Justin who has evicted her from his flat after getting involved with another woman. She is an assistant editor for a niche independent DIY and crafts publisher, overworked and paid a pittance. Her star client author is Katherin, a woman who writes books on the art of crocheting, and who will do nothing without Tiffy in attendance. Tiffy is supported by her friends, counsellor Mo and hotshot barrister, Gerty, and fellow workmate, Rachel. It gradually begins to emerge that Tiffy's relationship with Justin was a much darker and murkier affair as Tiffy begins to experience disturbing feelings and flashbacks. Upset and slowly beginning to recognise that she was a victim of emotional abuse, she is startled to discover just how much Gerty and Mo hated Justin for what he was doing to her, but had kept silent, knowing Tiffy would never have listened to them. Leon is familiar with emotional abuse, having seen his mother experience it at the hands of the type of men she chose as he was growing up. <br /><br />Beth O'Leary writes a captivating novel that shines thanks to her stellar characterisation, you cannot help but fall for Tiffy and Leon, and the brilliant supporting cast of Richie, Gerty, Mo and Rachel. Then there are Leon's terminal patients at the hospice, for whom Leon will do anything, like embarking on finding the lost love of the crocheting Mr Robert Prior, and the young, feisty Holly, smart enough to intuit she is Leon's favourite patient, despite him never saying it. This is such an appealing, fun and entertaining read, whilst touching on the most serious of issues of abuse and miscarriages of justice. Highly recommended. Many thanks to Quercus for an ARC.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14416026680012505172" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2878401641" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10062386857773622484">I should have known from the blurb on the front cover saying: “The new Jojo Moyes” that this book was not gonna be my thing. This is a contemporary romance novel about this girl Tiffy who’s boyfriends breaks up with her and she needs a place to live, so she moves into this apartment where Leon lives. Leon is a nurse and he works at night and he only uses the bed/apartment during the day so he needs a roommate to help him pay rent, and so Tiffy moves in and they share the same bed but they’ve nev</span>
  <span id="freeText10062386857773622484" style="display:none">I should have known from the blurb on the front cover saying: “The new Jojo Moyes” that this book was not gonna be my thing. This is a contemporary romance novel about this girl Tiffy who’s boyfriends breaks up with her and she needs a place to live, so she moves into this apartment where Leon lives. Leon is a nurse and he works at night and he only uses the bed/apartment during the day so he needs a roommate to help him pay rent, and so Tiffy moves in and they share the same bed but they’ve never met.<br /><br /><b>This book had an interesting premise which is what made me want to read it</b> - along with exceptional reviews from so many of my book friends. I thought I would love this. These characters are so dull and boring and this story is so dull and boring. Leon’s chapters are written in such a strange, unnecessary way, and the different between these two writing styles between their chapters was jarring and hard to get used to. His chapters have no quotes around the dialogue and it feels so choppy and clunky. I wasn’t a a fan of that writing style at all. Not to mention his character is so uninteresting and you know nothing about him besides his strange work hours, his needy girlfriend and his brother who’s in prison. <br /><br />I feel like these two main characters spend the first half of this book not being able to get over their annoying douche bag exes, and they talk about them constantly and I was just frustrated. And then after the halfway point things started to get really cheesy for me and I just rolled my eyes a lot. This does read kind of like a Jojo Moyes romance so if you enjoy that author you’ll probably love this but I personally did not, and I honestly don’t understand the hype surrounding this book? What is so great about it? Did I miss something? 😅<br /><br />This is my 4th book completed for the reading rush, for the challenge: read an authors debut book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10062386857773622484" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3600395841" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3600395841" />
    <a title="Michael David" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43787758-michael-david"><img alt="Michael David" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588459700p2/43787758.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3600395841?book_show_action=true">Oct 18, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael David" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael David" href="/user/show/43787758-michael-david">Michael David</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/41393171-the-flatshare">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3600395841" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6515129080630439058">This fun and heartfelt novel, from the author of The Switch, is just what I never knew I needed to read this weekend. <br/><br/>Tiffy needs a place to stay, pronto. Her ex-boyfriend is kicking her out of his home. With little money and a fragile heart, she decides to do a flatshare. Essentially, she will move into Leon’s flat, share the living room area, share the kitchen, share the bathroom, and share a bed. <br/><br/>Before your dirty mind hits the gutter, just know that the intention is that they will never meet</span>
  <span id="freeText6515129080630439058" style="display:none">This fun and heartfelt novel, from the author of The Switch, is just what I never knew I needed to read this weekend. <br /><br />Tiffy needs a place to stay, pronto. Her ex-boyfriend is kicking her out of his home. With little money and a fragile heart, she decides to do a flatshare. Essentially, she will move into Leon’s flat, share the living room area, share the kitchen, share the bathroom, and share a bed. <br /><br />Before your dirty mind hits the gutter, just know that the intention is that they will never meet. Leon works night as a hospice nurse, and stays with his girlfriend on weekends. It should work out perfectly! <br /><br />Tiffy and Leon’s friendship blossoms through post-it notes that they leave each other (my favorite part about the book. So fun and cute), and occasionally, food that they make for each other. <br /><br />This romantic comedy is sweet, with a surprising amount of depth. It was an absolute joy to read from the first page to the last (although the way Leon’s chapters are written were a bit difficult to get into at first). <br /><br />I laughed out loud at least a dozen times. I teared up a few times. I smiled hard many times. This book has an amazing cast of characters, including Tiffy’s friends and Leon’s imprisoned brother. <br /><br />5 stars, and I really hope the film world knows about Beth O’Leary’s novels. They would make phenomenal films!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6515129080630439058" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2979738814" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2979738814" />
    <a title="Larry H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h"><img alt="Larry H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577826084p2/5872506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2979738814?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Larry H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Larry H" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h">Larry H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2979738814" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5930773708081129194">4.5 stars.<br/><br/>This book was just sweet and fun and it made me happy!<br/><br/>Tiffy is in need of a place to live, since she’s lived in her ex-boyfriend’s apartment for far too long, even after he’d begun dating someone else. But since she’s in a low-paying job, there aren’t a lot of options, so a flatshare opportunity makes the most sense.<br/><br/>Leon is a hospice nurse who works nights, and she works days, so they’ll literally never see each other, which is what convinces her to take this opportunity, even if it me</span>
  <span id="freeText5930773708081129194" style="display:none">4.5 stars.<br /><br />This book was just sweet and fun and it made me happy!<br /><br />Tiffy is in need of a place to live, since she’s lived in her ex-boyfriend’s apartment for far too long, even after he’d begun dating someone else. But since she’s in a low-paying job, there aren’t a lot of options, so a flatshare opportunity makes the most sense.<br /><br />Leon is a hospice nurse who works nights, and she works days, so they’ll literally never see each other, which is what convinces her to take this opportunity, even if it means sleeping in Leon’s bed (although never with him). Leon's no-nonsense girlfriend Kay handles the transaction, thus ensuring Tiffy and Leon don't even meet. And since Leon will be spending weekends with Kay, there's no reason for any interaction.<br /><br />The two interact via post-it notes and memos, which grow from basic requests to much more personal conversations. And as each deals with their own crises—Tiffy’s ex can’t seem to let go and is becoming increasingly more possessive, and Leon’s brother is in prison for a crime he didn’t commit—amazingly, they are each other’s greatest support, despite having never met each other.<br /><br />When a missed alarm clock leads to their meet-cute (and meet-wet), they begin to fall for each other. Tiffy brings a free-spiritedness to Leon’s methodical ways, and Leon helps stabilize Tiffy, especially as she begins to realize how much harm her former boyfriend was causing her.<br /><br />Can love flourish when two people spend more time apart than together, and when they’re so different from one another? When you’ve been hurt before, can you let someone else in and let down your guard?<br /><br />I really enjoyed this book. Sure, it was predictable, but it was just so (to use a British colloquialism) lovely. At first I was a little off-put at Leon’s way of speaking when he narrated, but ultimately it fit perfectly with his personality. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>The Flatshare</i>
</b> explored some important issues plus it charmed me completely. It was more than a typical rom-com but yet it never aspired to be anything lofty, just a good story. Can you ask for anything more?<br /><br />See all of my reviews at <a href="http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com</a>.<br /><br />Check out my list of the best books I read in 2018 at <a href="https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2019/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2018.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2019/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2018.html</a>. <br /><br />You can follow me on Instagram at <a href="https://www.instagram.com/the.bookishworld.of.yrralh/" target="”_blank”" rel="nofollow noopener"> https://www.instagram.com/the.bookishworld.of.yrralh/.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5930773708081129194" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2838299224" />
    <a title="Christy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11284813-christy"><img alt="Christy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594293998p2/11284813.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2838299224?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy" href="/user/show/11284813-christy">Christy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/44347611-the-flatshare">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11284813-christy?shelf=2019-audio">2019-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11284813-christy?shelf=2019-five-stars">2019-five-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2838299224" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer346373846161047882"><b>5 stars</b><br/><br/><a href='https://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%2011/1208F527-6EDE-441C-8B8E-CBB870BC8566_zpsepf82ftx.png.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1562336248i/27774090._SY540_.png' alt=' photo 1208F527-6EDE-441C-8B8E-CBB870BC8566_zpsepf82ftx.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>I almost can’t believe that <i>The Flatshare</i> is a debut novel. Beth O’Leary delivered an original and fun to read romance that I adored.<br/><br/>Tiffy is looking for a place to live in London after another break up with her on again, off again ex-boyfriend Justin. The problem is, she can’t afford much. When she sees an ad for a Flatshare with a guy who works nights and is away on weekends, she jumps at it. Even if it does seem a bit odd at first. <br/><br/>Leon is a hospice nurse who works nights and is lo</span>
  <span id="freeText346373846161047882" style="display:none"><b>5 stars</b><br><br><a href="https://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%2011/1208F527-6EDE-441C-8B8E-CBB870BC8566_zpsepf82ftx.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1562336248i/27774090._SY540_.png" alt=" photo 1208F527-6EDE-441C-8B8E-CBB870BC8566_zpsepf82ftx.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I almost can’t believe that <i>The Flatshare</i> is a debut novel. Beth O’Leary delivered an original and fun to read romance that I adored.<br><br>Tiffy is looking for a place to live in London after another break up with her on again, off again ex-boyfriend Justin. The problem is, she can’t afford much. When she sees an ad for a Flatshare with a guy who works nights and is away on weekends, she jumps at it. Even if it does seem a bit odd at first. <br><br>Leon is a hospice nurse who works nights and is looking for some extra cash to help his brother. Renting out his flat is a quick and easy way to make it. He and Tiffy share the flat and the bed and even though they haven’t met in person, they quickly get to know each other.<br><br>The notes they write back and forth are adorable. It was one of my favorite things about this story. I loved the build up and the anticipation of when they would finally meet. And let me tell you... their first meeting didn’t disappoint.<br><br>Both Tiffy and Leon were exceptional characters. There were also some great secondary characters (Leon’s brother being my favorite). This book is a lovely romance, but it’s more than that. It’s a story of finding yourself and coming into your own. It’s beautiful, unique and complex. <br><br>I listened to the audio version of this story and the narrators were great. It was easy to listen to, well Tiffy’s chapters anyways. Leon’s chapters were hard to get used to. They’re written differently and are very choppy. It was difficult to get past that at first, but by the end I hardly noticed. <br><br><i>The Flatshare </i> is a sweet and charming romance, but it also has a good bit of emotion and deals with some heavier topics <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ an emotionally abusive/manipulative/stalker ex-boyfriend <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Overall, I truly loved it. I can’t wait to read more from this author!<br><i>
  <blockquote>“It was never home until you were there, Tiffy.”</blockquote>
</i></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_2862645028" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2862645028" />
    <a title="Jayme" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11345366-jayme"><img alt="Jayme" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545654456p2/11345366.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2862645028?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jayme" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jayme" href="/user/show/11345366-jayme">Jayme</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11345366-jayme?shelf=women-s-fiction">women-s-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11345366-jayme?shelf=rom_com">rom_com</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2862645028" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7653937493211503291">Although I generally read and review, “Mystery and Suspense” novels, it doesn’t mean that I don’t occasionally enjoy seeing a Romantic Comedy in the theater, 🍿, or reading one when I just need a “feel good” story! <br/><br/>I needed one this week. And, I am happy to say that this book did not let me down! <br/><br/><br/>Tiffy Moore needed a cheap place to live. <br/><br/>Leon Twomey needed some extra money.<br/><br/>The problem: He lives in a flat that has just one bedroom, and one bed. <br/><br/>The Solution: He will live there by day (he works nig</span>
  <span id="freeText7653937493211503291" style="display:none">Although I generally read and review, “Mystery and Suspense” novels, it doesn’t mean that I don’t occasionally enjoy seeing a Romantic Comedy in the theater, 🍿, or reading one when I just need a “feel good” story! <br /><br />I needed one this week. And, I am happy to say that this book did not let me down! <br /><br /><br />Tiffy Moore needed a cheap place to live. <br /><br />Leon Twomey needed some extra money.<br /><br />The problem: He lives in a flat that has just one bedroom, and one bed. <br /><br />The Solution: He will live there by day (he works nights as a palliative care nurse) and his new flat mate can live there by night. The two will even take turns using the same bed, since they will be in it at separate times! 🛌<br /><br />Yep, you read that right! <br /><br />Leon’s girlfriend, Kay, isn’t wild about the idea-so she will be in charge of interviewing and approving Leon’s new flatmate. Her rule: Leon and Tiffy are never to be in the flat at the same time. In fact, only Kay will meet Tiffy prior to her moving in. <br /><br />The book is told from the alternating perspectives of Leon and Tiffy, as they get to know each other by sharing their thoughts on those sticky “ post it “ notes, ( fun to read!) and by leaving food for one another! ☕️<br /><br />A great cast of supporting characters provide equally compelling sub plots, which I will let you discover on your own. <br /><br />If you are looking for a romance without graphic sex scenes, which will make you smile, laugh, and root for the characters to get their “happily ever after” endings, I recommend you add this one to your TBR list! <br /><br />One of my favorites in this genre, for 2019 !!<br /><br />By the way...does anyone besides LEON have a good recipe for mushroom stroganoff?? It sounded so yummy! 😋</span>
  <a data-text-id="7653937493211503291" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2793742583?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Umut Rados" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Umut Rados" href="/user/show/24816039-umut-rados">Umut Rados</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24816039-umut-rados?shelf=favorites-2019">favorites-2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2793742583" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13624040086827629326">Let's cut it short if you don't want to read the whole review. If you like to read contemporary feel good books that'll cheer you up, chick-lits, light spring/summer reads, you MUST read this book. It's a very good example of its kind that I haven't seen in a long time as a Sophie Kinsella fan. <br/>On the cover it says the new Jojo Moyes. As far as I'm concerned, this is much better! And, it's not a depressive book under the shelter of its umbrella. <br/><br/>When I opened the book and started to read about T</span>
  <span id="freeText13624040086827629326" style="display:none">Let's cut it short if you don't want to read the whole review. If you like to read contemporary feel good books that'll cheer you up, chick-lits, light spring/summer reads, you MUST read this book. It's a very good example of its kind that I haven't seen in a long time as a Sophie Kinsella fan. <br />On the cover it says the new Jojo Moyes. As far as I'm concerned, this is much better! And, it's not a depressive book under the shelter of its umbrella. <br /><br />When I opened the book and started to read about Tiffy, this immediately gave me Sophie Kinsella vibes. I LOVE Sophie Kinsella, she’s the sun of my gloomy days. Any time you feel bad, pick up a book of hers, and it’ll cheer you up. But, as I moved on, it got actually more emotional than I anticipated. Also, there’s definitely more to this book than traditional chick-lit romantic comedies. Race, controlling relationships, and backstories of these characters made it actually deeper and richer than I expected. However, the writing and the way O’Leary brought these subjects to life doesn’t make you gloomy at all. It comes to the surface very authentically and organically. Not depressive AT ALL. Plus, the jokes and humour is always there to make you smile every now and then 🙂<br /><br />The set up of the story is what I loved the most. Tiffy and Leon never see each other as they live in the same flat at different times. I think it was a difficult task for the writer too, to develop a relationship through post-it notes that they start to leave to each other. It was very interesting and very well done.<br />All in all, it was a really easy going, bright, yet emotional read that I enjoyed a lot. Would definitely recommend it these Spring days.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13624040086827629326" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9619239952350033753">Totes Adorbs.<br/><br/><b>If you’re in need of a light, sweet rom com that will pick you up when you’re feeling down, grab “The Flatshare” by Beth O’Leary - it hits all the right notes.</b><br/><br/>Tiffy and Leon become Flatmates in the most unusual of ways. Leon, you see, works nights and Tiffy works days so they stay in the apartment in shifts, with Leon having it during the day and Tiffy on nights and weekends. The two communicate only by post-it notes and learn all about each other’s lives that way, hearing funny, qu</span>
  <span id="freeText9619239952350033753" style="display:none">Totes Adorbs.<br /><br /><b>If you’re in need of a light, sweet rom com that will pick you up when you’re feeling down, grab “The Flatshare” by Beth O’Leary - it hits all the right notes.</b><br /><br />Tiffy and Leon become Flatmates in the most unusual of ways. Leon, you see, works nights and Tiffy works days so they stay in the apartment in shifts, with Leon having it during the day and Tiffy on nights and weekends. The two communicate only by post-it notes and learn all about each other’s lives that way, hearing funny, quirky stories, and lamenting about life. Somehow the two forge a relationship even though they’ve never laid eyes on each other.<br /><br />Sounds impossible right? Here, somehow, the impossible becomes sweet, soulful and just plain perfect. <br /><br /><b>With a few hilarious moments thrown in, this novel is utter perfection, which I highly recommend.</b><br /><br />A huge thank you to my local library for loaning me a copy of the audiobook.<br /><br />Published on Goodreads on 11.8.20.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2798475173" />
    <a title="EmBibliophile" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/62566585-embibliophile"><img alt="EmBibliophile" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1551380716p2/62566585.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2798475173?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="EmBibliophile" class="user" itemprop="url" name="EmBibliophile" href="/user/show/62566585-embibliophile">EmBibliophile</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/44017619-the-flatshare">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/62566585-embibliophile?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2798475173" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10502532361290965420"><b>3.5<br/><br/>‘Tiffy & Leon share a flat. Tiffy & Leon share a bed. Tiffy & Leon have never met.’</b><br/><br/>That was such a unique adorable book.<br/><br/>To be honest, I almost gave up on it. I couldn’t get over how annoying the chapters in Leon’s POV were written. I was so frustrated, and couldn’t see the point in it. But then I see hope in the book and I decided to keep going. <br/><br/>Also because the cover is gorgeous! It would be a shame to give up on a book with a cover like that.<br/><br/>Tiffy and Leon have an unusual agreement. Those t</span>
  <span id="freeText10502532361290965420" style="display:none"><b>3.5<br /><br />‘Tiffy &amp; Leon share a flat. Tiffy &amp; Leon share a bed. Tiffy &amp; Leon have never met.’</b><br /><br />That was such a unique adorable book.<br /><br />To be honest, I almost gave up on it. I couldn’t get over how annoying the chapters in Leon’s POV were written. I was so frustrated, and couldn’t see the point in it. But then I see hope in the book and I decided to keep going. <br /><br />Also because the cover is gorgeous! It would be a shame to give up on a book with a cover like that.<br /><br />Tiffy and Leon have an unusual agreement. Those two are desperate enough to share a flat, or actually a bed, to be more specific. The thing is, they have never met. The plan was that Tiffy would have the flat by night and Leon would have it by day. They started communicating via post it notes -which was adorable, I loved those notes so much- but then their life which has been separate for too long started to intertwine.<br /><br /><b>’Look,’ he says, ‘have you ever looked forward to reading a book so much you can’t actually start it?’</b><br /><br />It took me a lot to finish the first 30% of the book. After that i couldn’t stop. It was so good. Really adorable. And has great relatable characters. Even though I was annoyed by how Leon’s chapters were written, I started to see the point. It suited his character really well. All the relationships in this book were perfect. I Loved Leon and Richie’s relationship. Tiffy and her friends have the most supporting loving friendship. Also, Leon and Tiffy were so cute and he was so damn understanding and caring. This was an adorable fluffy chick-lit book that also deals with some heavy material like emotional abuse, gaslighting, and stalking.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10502532361290965420" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2853390795" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2853390795" />
    <a title="Jacob Proffitt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1331641-jacob-proffitt"><img alt="Jacob Proffitt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325699498p2/1331641.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2853390795?book_show_action=true">Aug 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jacob Proffitt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jacob Proffitt" href="/user/show/1331641-jacob-proffitt">Jacob Proffitt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1331641-jacob-proffitt?shelf=unfinished">unfinished</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2853390795" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10783056091471859529">I'm going to be an outlier on this one because it just left me cold. Tiffy is a weak idiot who longs for her ex even though he has treated her like crap. By the third time her friends had to talk her out of making romantic overtures to him I was just done. It doesn't help that she is working a job that pays next to zero and where she's obviously not taken seriously. So she's weak on all fronts, is what I'm saying. I found her pathetic and just couldn't face a whole novel of her whingeing.<br/><br/>Leon is</span>
  <span id="freeText10783056091471859529" style="display:none">I'm going to be an outlier on this one because it just left me cold. Tiffy is a weak idiot who longs for her ex even though he has treated her like crap. By the third time her friends had to talk her out of making romantic overtures to him I was just done. It doesn't help that she is working a job that pays next to zero and where she's obviously not taken seriously. So she's weak on all fronts, is what I'm saying. I found her pathetic and just couldn't face a whole novel of her whingeing.<br /><br />Leon is a different problem. He's with a woman and spends all weekend with her and I kind of hate it in a romance where one of the leads I'm supposed to root for is in a sexual relationship with someone else during the story. He's not only in a sexual relationship, but they've practically moved in together, only not actually moved in together in what feels like a contrivance just to have the story. I mean, if he can spend all weekend, why aren't they just moving in together? And then you get his brother in jail for a crime he didn't commit and it's obvious that there's something hinky going on with that and I wish I could care but given what I've experienced from the author so far I give it even odds that it's something stupid and/or "original" that I'm supposed to get outraged by at some point.<br /><br />Only the worst thing about Leon is that his sections are written in this format that's half script, half shorthand with lots of subjects cut out so you have to assume them from context. It's "clever", is what I'm saying and I can't help thinking that the author is very proud of herself for giving his sections a unique "feel" and I spent the whole time thinking "I know you think you're clever, but this pretentious crap isn't adding anything to the story and only works to call attention to itself." I hate when the form takes over the story and this is the stylistic equivalent of a child whose parents have told it how smart it is all its life so it spends every moment in public making portentous comments about recycling and the environment and how meat is murder.<br /><br />So yeah, I was turned off by practically everything and I gave up. I liked their notes once they started, not least because it meant less of the pretentious claptrap that was usually Leon's sections. I still can't get away from Tiffy being a sniveling wimp and Leon being <strong>already in a committed relationship</strong> and thus preventing me from rooting for him to make a connection with his flatmate. So yeah, not enough improvement to keep me engaged.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10783056091471859529" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3399806202" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3399806202" />
    <a title="Ankita Barik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59827021-ankita-barik"><img alt="Ankita Barik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586355554p2/59827021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3399806202?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ankita Barik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ankita Barik" href="/user/show/59827021-ankita-barik">Ankita Barik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/41150287-the-flatshare">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3399806202" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13163628916708091740">This is undoubtedly the most unique story I have read off lately. The narrative is inclusive, keeping in mind the personality of the two protagonists, which I found to be totally refreshing and engrossing. <br/><br/>When it is Tiffy's chapter, the narrative is verbose, quirky and loud with emotions. And when it switches to Leon, it is crisp, thoughtful and guarded. It was like reading their minds talk through their chapters. This kind of narrative gives the reader a real glance at the emotions, the charac</span>
  <span id="freeText13163628916708091740" style="display:none">This is undoubtedly the most unique story I have read off lately. The narrative is inclusive, keeping in mind the personality of the two protagonists, which I found to be totally refreshing and engrossing. <br /><br />When it is Tiffy's chapter, the narrative is verbose, quirky and loud with emotions. And when it switches to Leon, it is crisp, thoughtful and guarded. It was like reading their minds talk through their chapters. This kind of narrative gives the reader a real glance at the emotions, the characters are processing simultaneously, in a way akin to their nature. There is also no awkward disconnect as the narrative style shifts, it's written very seamlessly. Kudos to Beth for that!! I disagree when it's said that she is the next Jojo Moyes. She is just being Beth. Fabulously. <br /><br />Personally, I enjoyed Leon's chapters more. There is something about a quiet, brooding man who suddenly finds himself sharing alot more than usual, very adorable. Also communicating through notes and post-its in the time of WhatsApp, as a means of getting to know each other, is super cute in a very yesteryear letter writing romance kind of a way. <br /><br />I grinned at every smart comeback of Tiffy and sharp observational humor of Leon. I especially liked the remark about Jägerbomb (which is absolutely spot on btw) - fundamentally disgusting but leaves a delicious aftereffect on the dance floor. <br /><br />Definitely worth the binge read. Emanates the vibe of an old world charm in the new age romance novel. Leaves you feeling warm, fuzzy and full of giggles.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13163628916708091740" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3080915065" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3080915065" />
    <a title="Anne Bogel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7494963-anne-bogel"><img alt="Anne Bogel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560950142p2/7494963.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3080915065?book_show_action=true">Dec 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne Bogel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne Bogel" href="/user/show/7494963-anne-bogel">Anne Bogel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3080915065" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1648394589836239385">I read this entire novel in one sitting on a Sunday afternoon; it's a romantic comedy that manages to tackle serious issues while maintaining a light and breezy feel. Don't miss the backstory on how the author's personal life inspired the premise, and how she managed to write nearly every word of the 320-page novel on her own commute in and out of London. There are a few spicy scenes but this romance is mostly closed-door.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('01kcLLD76ZxZ3u34AttojFzOyFeHfSpiqcuUqdqX70BJkMtVgTPGD57rQM+vuguQxyZf8PIYwC0xWyZiHS2ATQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ANf/nyq8PqZ2hdX1N0LB94uq6BVSux6GMaTKaTAKx5qaHijmG3QRNbGweMKaI6LrEEJ/sife9MmpNHii97Colw==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15044093298899388973">Beth studied English at university before going into children’s publishing. She lives as close to the countryside as she can get while still being within reach of London, and wrote her first novel, The Flatshare, on her train journey to and from work.<br/>You’ll usually find her curled up with a book, a cup of tea, and several woolly jumpers (whatever the weather).<br/> </span>
